    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_2068742417" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068742417" />
    <a title="Kristina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4272284-kristina"><img alt="Kristina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584248335p2/4272284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2068742417?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina" href="/user/show/4272284-kristina">Kristina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=loved-em">loved-em</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=my-book">my-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=graphic-novel-comics">graphic-novel-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4272284-kristina?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068742417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18169296632046378739">I can always depend on Calvin and Hobbes to lighten the mood and provide lots of laughs. <i>Weirdos From Another Planet!</i> is one of the many books in my Calvin and Hobbes collection. I really should read them more often. Calvin is a wonderful mix of an incredibly intelligent six-year-old boy who can ask about the meaning of life and yet still enjoy hours of cartoons on tv while eating his favorite cereal, Sugar-Coated Chocolate Bombs. Hobbes, his constant companion, sometimes tries to steer Calvin t</span>
  <span id="freeText18169296632046378739" style="display:none">I can always depend on Calvin and Hobbes to lighten the mood and provide lots of laughs. <i>Weirdos From Another Planet!</i> is one of the many books in my Calvin and Hobbes collection. I really should read them more often. Calvin is a wonderful mix of an incredibly intelligent six-year-old boy who can ask about the meaning of life and yet still enjoy hours of cartoons on tv while eating his favorite cereal, Sugar-Coated Chocolate Bombs. Hobbes, his constant companion, sometimes tries to steer Calvin towards making smarter choices, but usually they both end up doing something awful (wrecking havoc in the living room by playing baseball). Is Hobbes imaginary? Is he real? I say he’s a magical tiger who comes alive when alone with Calvin. I think we could all use a little Hobbes in our lives. <br /><br />I don’t want to make Calvin &amp; Hobbes political (in fact, I pulled it from the shelf because I knew it wouldn’t be), but there’s an ongoing joke throughout this collection that is eerily well-suited to Trump’s administration. Calvin tells his father that if he wants to be re-elected to the office of Dad, he has to bring up his poll numbers. He tells his father: “your recognition factor is high [but] the scandals of your administration continue to haunt you.” He continues to advise his father: “See, your record in office is miserable and the character issue is killing you…if anyone ever needed a slick ad campaign, it’s you. I think the image we need to create for you is, ‘repentant, but learning.’ You know, show some humility, and present yourself as a regular guy trying to learn the ropes of a difficult job” (28). Whenever Trump screws up (which is often), his supporters and apologists say this very same thing: “Uh, it’s a tough job and he has a steep learning curve.” Really? Being President of the USA is difficult? Who woulda thought….? Anyway, when I read these panels, I immediately saw their relevancy to the current political climate. Of course, the scandals Calvin’s dad is dealing with are “homeworkgate” and “bedtimegate.” Much more benign than potentially treasonous collusion with Russia.<br /><br />What really made me laugh like a loon (in public!) were the panels describing Calvin trying to be helpful by fixing a leaking faucet but not turning the water off first. As the bathroom is flooding, he’s walking downstairs to get as many buckets as he can find. He’s not pictured in the panels, just his parents, and the expressions on their faces gradually get more alarmed as they listen to him: “Nothing’s wrong…da dee doo ba…I just want a bucket to hold some…stuff…Let’s see, how many buckets do we have? Dum de doo…No cause for alarm…No need to panic…I just want a few buckets. La la” (80). I love Calvin. Of course when Dad comes running upstairs and sees the mess, Calvin blames Hobbes. What a great friend. <br /><br />Anyway, if you need some laughter, I recommend anything Calvin &amp; Hobbes. They’re delightful. Many thanks to Bill Watterson for creating them. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18169296632046378739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I have always been an ardent lover of Bill Watterson's creativity, passion and beautiful sense of values which has taught(still teaching) the wonder beneath the quotidian life. <br/><br/>This book is a valued possession which I know that I would cherish for a lifetime(and perhaps add it in my Will and pass it on to the next generations to come).</span>

<div id="review_341116089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341116089" />
    <a title="Sam Ang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9122062-sam-ang"><img alt="Sam Ang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335625233p2/9122062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341116089?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Ang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Ang" href="/user/show/9122062-sam-ang">Sam Ang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9122062-sam-ang?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9122062-sam-ang?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9122062-sam-ang?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341116089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7696966929676564520">The full article of the review is available in this link:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookunderthesun.blogspot.sg/2011/07/calvin-and-hobbes-weirdos-from-another.html'>http://bookunderthesun.blogspot.sg/20...</a><br/><br/><br/>Ever read the comic in pullout section of the newspaper? If you did, then Calvin and Hobbes will not be total strangers to you. The humorous comic which ran in boxes of four or sometimes luxuriously filling up half of the page had been featured in most comic sections for as far as I can read, and had been the company of most readers of newspaper. There are a few compilations of Calvin and Hobbes comi</span>
  <span id="freeText7696966929676564520" style="display:none">The full article of the review is available in this link:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookunderthesun.blogspot.sg/2011/07/calvin-and-hobbes-weirdos-from-another.html">http://bookunderthesun.blogspot.sg/20...</a><br /><br /><br />Ever read the comic in pullout section of the newspaper? If you did, then Calvin and Hobbes will not be total strangers to you. The humorous comic which ran in boxes of four or sometimes luxuriously filling up half of the page had been featured in most comic sections for as far as I can read, and had been the company of most readers of newspaper. There are a few compilations of Calvin and Hobbes comics and Weirdos from Another Planet! is one of them.<br /><br />Calvin was by no means crazy, just an imaginative kid who spends most of his intellect trying to get his own way with his family and friends, not unlike what most of us did in our childhood. His mischievous yet creative ways always made me laughed, and along with Hobbes, he made the people around him crawl up the wall literally. In our childhood, how many of us did not spend time trying to think of a way or excuse trying to bend the adults' reasoning to our side in order to get that piece of dessert that we longed for? And how many of them ended up not knowing whether they should be mad or they should laugh?<br /><br />A praise to Watterson: the ironic and funny monologues and conversations usually carried with them the reality of the world. For example, Calvin decided to leave Earth for Mars because he came to the conclusion that adults were leaving the Earth dirty so that the next generation will clean up after them.<br /><br />The art used in the comics is also varied, with different styles meant for different imagined scenario. Watterson's style preferred the simple, with buttoned eyes and a few strokes to get the statement across the comic. In dramatic moments, he leaned heavily to exaggerated styles, with large eyes and hairs that stood upright to show shock, and large gaping mouth to show anger.<br /><br />The collection really did make my evening more enjoyable, and I still took it out to read once in a while although I had read it numerous times. Calvin and Hobbes: Weirdos from Another Planet! is definitely a recommended reading for you when you are down and depressed.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7696966929676564520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590441643" href="/book/show/70495.Weirdos_From_Another_Planet_Calvin_and_Hobbes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=humour-parody">humour-parody</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64838962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11879777333257699111">Calvin is one kid that no one would ever want to try to raise, and Hobbes is one (stuffed) tiger that no one would ever want to mess with. But these two always have their fun, and they sure do have a hell of a lot of adventures (mostly with Calvin's parents): camping, going to the zoo, digging for dinosaur bones, going to Mars, being lifted up in the stratosphere by a balloon, fixing the bathroom sink among others. The list is always endless with this duo. There are tons of philosophical, satiri</span>
  <span id="freeText11879777333257699111" style="display:none">Calvin is one kid that no one would ever want to try to raise, and Hobbes is one (stuffed) tiger that no one would ever want to mess with. But these two always have their fun, and they sure do have a hell of a lot of adventures (mostly with Calvin's parents): camping, going to the zoo, digging for dinosaur bones, going to Mars, being lifted up in the stratosphere by a balloon, fixing the bathroom sink among others. The list is always endless with this duo. There are tons of philosophical, satirical, ironic, and even slapstick humor all around. Calvin counters with words as relevant today as in 1988, because, <i>"Life's a lot more fun when you're not responsible for your actions." </i><br /><br />This collection of cartoons is funny, imaginative and is an exaggerated view of the life of a child. There is no question in my mind that Watterson was an imaginative child and probably got in a lot of serious trouble during that time. We should be grateful for that, as he grew up to be an outstanding cartoonist and this book proof of that. <br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Weirdos From Another Planet! (Calvin and Hobbes)<br /><u>Author</u> Bill Watterson<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>

    <a title="Evelyn Woagh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23937964-evelyn-woagh"><img alt="Evelyn Woagh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516145133p2/23937964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/775427844?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn Woagh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn Woagh" href="/user/show/23937964-evelyn-woagh">Evelyn Woagh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23937964-evelyn-woagh?shelf=my-actual-bookshelf">my-actual-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775427844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14939107733019451426">As similar to my review of the previous Calvin and Hobbes (seen here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://goo.gl/rTv1z7'>http://goo.gl/rTv1z7</a>), there were several instances of food-related humour it could do without. Surprisingly, the parents' reception to Calvin's behaviour was less implicitly violent and more of the type of "Family Jokes" that annoy me to the point of cringing. Preferable to the "Threats Joke" that was prevalent in "It's a Magical World."<br/><br/>The cover is wonderful, and immediately drew me in-to read through it, as it's been a whil</span>
  <span id="freeText14939107733019451426" style="display:none">As similar to my review of the previous Calvin and Hobbes (seen here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://goo.gl/rTv1z7">http://goo.gl/rTv1z7</a>), there were several instances of food-related humour it could do without. Surprisingly, the parents' reception to Calvin's behaviour was less implicitly violent and more of the type of "Family Jokes" that annoy me to the point of cringing. Preferable to the "Threats Joke" that was prevalent in "It's a Magical World."<br /><br />The cover is wonderful, and immediately drew me in-to read through it, as it's been a while since I've seen this one. The colours are wonderful and implies a fun story. Nonetheless, as with my major criticism of the series, cool and imaginative stories in C&amp;H tend to be too short, as the same with the Mars Trip one. The cover stood out to me on the bookshelf, in stark contrast to the more disturbingly titled one "Attack of the Deranged Mutant Killer Monster Snow Goons" which I decided against reading.<br /><br />Also interesting this time, whether by my own evolving perceptions, or by the writer's content, this collection more clearly covers the concept that this boy's imagination, along with his tiger friend, are driven to such hilarious heights because of the existentialist crisis that comes out of Suburbia. With everyone remaining in their homes, far from cultural hotspots, and focused heavily on the dream of working all day and coming home to do nothing/watch tv, Calvin -while sometimes more interested in tv- seeks out alternative sources of existential stimulation found in his adventures with Hobbes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14939107733019451426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10938107307409438475" style="display:none">"Hi I'm wondering if you sell kegs of dynamite." I love this quote because it shows how imaginative Calvin is and how funny he is.<br /><br />I love Hobbes because he is so civil and normal. Calvin is not normal and even though Hobbes is a form of Calvin's imagination, they are so different. I love how Hobbes thinks tigers are the best.<br /><br />A theme i noticed in the book was just how rough life can be sometimes. Calvin recognizes life situations more then the normal 6 year old and he realizes how tough it can be sometimes and I thought that was deep. Calvin is only six yet he realizes how many challenges there are and how good it can be to have a friend. Hobbes is his life ling friend and they are both equally as smart and get through situations together.<br /><br />The overall feeling of the story is humor. The book is very funny an witty. Bill Watterson does a great job creating a character so innocent yet experienced. It was a very good book.</span>

<div id="review_3523491784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3523491784" />
    <a title="Bill Coffin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4288226-bill-coffin"><img alt="Bill Coffin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603941271p2/4288226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3523491784?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Coffin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Coffin" href="/user/show/4288226-bill-coffin">Bill Coffin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3523491784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17196098815794983174">One of the finest - if not the finest - newspaper strips in the last 40 years begins here, with this fourth collection of the entire Calvin & Hobbes run. Each of these collections gathers a year's worth of the strip, in which we follow six-year-old Calvin and his tiger companion Hobbes as they take us on a guided tour through youthful imagination, adventure, misbehavior, parents, bullies, teachers, babysitters, artistic expression, crushing on Susie Derkins, and more. We all know how this strip </span>
  <span id="freeText17196098815794983174" style="display:none">One of the finest - if not the finest - newspaper strips in the last 40 years begins here, with this fourth collection of the entire Calvin &amp; Hobbes run. Each of these collections gathers a year's worth of the strip, in which we follow six-year-old Calvin and his tiger companion Hobbes as they take us on a guided tour through youthful imagination, adventure, misbehavior, parents, bullies, teachers, babysitters, artistic expression, crushing on Susie Derkins, and more. We all know how this strip ended abruptly when it felt like it had so much more to give, but by ending when and how he did, creator Bill Watterson preserved his masterpiece in the best possible way, leaving us forever wanting more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17196098815794983174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3345734832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3345734832" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40614773-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465938112p2/40614773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3345734832?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/40614773-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40614773-bradley?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3345734832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6624592401101599695">Published in 1990, this collection of Watterson’s comics from 1988 feature the rambunctious six-year-old Calvin and his beloved tiger Hobbes as they explore the outer limits of their imaginations, well at least Calvin’s with his stuffed animal in tow. In this collection, the duo go camping, try to outwit Rosalyn the babysitter, and even set course for Mars in a little red wagon while often musing about human nature. Poignant and philosophical, reading this collection again for the first time in </span>
  <span id="freeText6624592401101599695" style="display:none">Published in 1990, this collection of Watterson’s comics from 1988 feature the rambunctious six-year-old Calvin and his beloved tiger Hobbes as they explore the outer limits of their imaginations, well at least Calvin’s with his stuffed animal in tow. In this collection, the duo go camping, try to outwit Rosalyn the babysitter, and even set course for Mars in a little red wagon while often musing about human nature. Poignant and philosophical, reading this collection again for the first time in over 20 years was comforting. Plus, I got some of the jokes this time around. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6624592401101599695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3543171834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3543171834" />
    <a title="Thomas Scholtes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2706186-thomas-scholtes"><img alt="Thomas Scholtes" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3543171834?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Scholtes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Scholtes" href="/user/show/2706186-thomas-scholtes">Thomas Scholtes</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3543171834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9403422434955992637">Exceptional writer and amazing cartoons with such a deep meaning and thinking structure for a comic strip.<br/><br/>Reading these really does take me back to being a kid again, relating and/or being horrified with Calvin's actions and thought process. But every strip is excellent, and having them consolidated and following through longer story arcs is just magical. I know all of these books will be 5 stars, because they each have something unique to offer, using just a few characters and the imagination o</span>
  <span id="freeText9403422434955992637" style="display:none">Exceptional writer and amazing cartoons with such a deep meaning and thinking structure for a comic strip.<br /><br />Reading these really does take me back to being a kid again, relating and/or being horrified with Calvin's actions and thought process. But every strip is excellent, and having them consolidated and following through longer story arcs is just magical. I know all of these books will be 5 stars, because they each have something unique to offer, using just a few characters and the imagination of a child.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183286844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6851291147523682495">Fun collection of Calvin & Hobbes from around 1988. I love the strips where Calvin is sharing his dad's "poll results," to see whether or not the dad can survive another "term" in Fatherhood. (Very fitting for 1988, too, as it was an election year). This is also the era when STUPENDOUS MAN is born, which becomes a stock Calvin motif throughout the duration of the comics.</span>
  <span id="freeText6851291147523682495" style="display:none">Fun collection of Calvin &amp; Hobbes from around 1988. I love the strips where Calvin is sharing his dad's "poll results," to see whether or not the dad can survive another "term" in Fatherhood. (Very fitting for 1988, too, as it was an election year). This is also the era when STUPENDOUS MAN is born, which becomes a stock Calvin motif throughout the duration of the comics.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Is5oD+WobAz9sOVG9BUSzvhbTHK8E1cKQsPgHKlM5hs/mkqRBo0efXofebtz6gqriYzm+IiFVzRNorxVScWBdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5Ze54oAMBJivoWgLKW+qA9fswvb3SARLIikRCRDlbpH4w5t8Yyl26SgO9PaukLJmpjtofMPeBHUtSE1A8GwJ/g==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13778.Bill_Watterson">About Bill Watterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13778.Bill_Watterson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1374016829p3/13778.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/13778.Bill_Watterson">Bill Watterson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,735
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12668635829308390271">Bill Watterson (born William Boyd Watterson II) is an American cartoonist, and the author of the comic strip "Calvin and Hobbes". His career as a syndicated cartoonist ran from 1985 to 1995; he stopped drawing "Calvin and Hobbes" at the end of 1995 with a short statement to newspaper editors and his fans that he felt he had achieved all he could in the comic strip medium. During the early years of</span>
  <span id="freeText12668635829308390271" style="display:none">Bill Watterson (born William Boyd Watterson II) is an American cartoonist, and the author of the comic strip "Calvin and Hobbes". His career as a syndicated cartoonist ran from 1985 to 1995; he stopped drawing "Calvin and Hobbes" at the end of 1995 with a short statement to newspaper editors and his fans that he felt he had achieved all he could in the comic strip medium. During the early years of his career he produced several drawings and additional contributions for "Target: The Political Cartoon Quarterly". Watterson is known for his views on licensing and comic syndication, as well as for his reclusive nature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12668635829308390271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
